
What we see is:

  * we can't cut further using our algorithm
  * unlike the end of June sparse model, this one is actually defective
    * the essential construction `(weight, ("accum-1-2", "dict-2", "eos", "char"))` is a serious algorithmic bug
    * only the fact that the training data is ultra-tiny allows the system to overfit to correct this bug
    * the training data need to be at least somewhat larger if we want reliable results 
  * before we could have cut `(0.016524186f0, ("accum-1-2", "dict-2", "eos", "char"))` and recover by retraining, but with a model this small one can't recover after cutting
    * conclusion: when "training saturation loss" rises after cutting a weight, this is not a good sign even when it rises a bit
